# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've traced the Rust trait obligation fulfillment chain through the rustc compiler, identifying **7 key files** and **9 critical symbols** that implement the obligation resolution system:

### Key Components:

1. **ObligationForest** (`compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`) - The foundational data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations as a forest of dependency trees

2. **FulfillmentContext** (`compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`) - Wraps the ObligationForest and manages the overall trait resolution process

3. **FulfillProcessor** (`compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`) - Implements the ObligationProcessor trait and bridges obligation forest processing with trait selection

4. **SelectionContext** (`compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs`) - The core engine that selects trait implementations for obligations

5. **Candidate Assembly** (`compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs`) - Collects possible trait implementations (impls, bounds, builtins)

6. **Candidate Confirmation** (`compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs`) - Validates selected candidates and collects nested obligations

7. **Error Reporting** (`compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs`) - Generates user-facing diagnostics for unsatisfied trait bounds

The complete flow shows how obligations cascade through the system: from registration → forest processing → selection → candidate assembly → confirmation → nested obligation generation → error reporting.

The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. The chain flows through several key components:\\n\\n1. **Obligation Forest (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)**: The foundational data structure that tracks outstanding obligations as a forest of trees. Each obligation can generate sub-obligations, forming a dependency graph. The ObligationForest manages the state of obligations (pending, completed, or error) and processes them recursively through process_obligations().\\n\\n2. **Fulfillment Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillmentContext wraps an ObligationForest and manages the trait resolution process. It maintains PendingPredicateObligations which combine a PredicateObligation with stalled type variables. The context provides register_obligation() to add new obligations and select() to process them.\\n\\n3. **Fulfill Processor (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillProcessor implements the ObligationProcessor trait and is the callback used during obligation forest processing. It bridges the obligation forest with the SelectionContext, processing each obligation through trait selection.\\n\\n4. **Selection Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs)**: The core selection engine that attempts to select a trait implementation for an obligation. It uses select() to find a matching implementation and returns SelectionResult which can be Ok(Some(selection)), Ok(None) for ambiguous cases, or Err for unsatisfied obligations.\\n\\n5. **Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)**: The assemble_candidates() method collects all possible implementations that could satisfy a trait obligation. The chain flows through several key components:\\n\\n1. **Obligation Forest (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)**: The foundational data structure that tracks outstanding obligations as a forest of trees. Each obligation can generate sub-obligations, forming a dependency graph. The ObligationForest manages the state of obligations (pending, completed, or error) and processes them recursively through process_obligations().\\n\\n2. **Fulfillment Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillmentContext wraps an ObligationForest and manages the trait resolution process. It maintains PendingPredicateObligations which combine a PredicateObligation with stalled type variables. The context provides register_obligation() to add new obligations and select() to process them.\\n\\n3. **Fulfill Processor (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillProcessor implements the ObligationProcessor trait and is the callback used during obligation forest processing. It bridges the obligation forest with the SelectionContext, processing each obligation through trait selection.\\n\\n4. **Selection Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs)**: The core selection engine that attempts to select a trait implementation for an obligation. It uses select() to find a matching implementation and returns SelectionResult which can be Ok(Some(selection)), Ok(None) for ambiguous cases, or Err for unsatisfied obligations.\\n\\n5. **Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)**: The assemble_candidates() method collects all possible implementations that could satisfy a trait obligation. It considers:\\n   - Explicit impls in scope\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - Builtin trait implementations (Sized, Copy, Clone, etc.)\\n   - Caller's where-clause bounds (param env candidates)\\n   - Auto trait implementations\\n\\n6. **Candidate Confirmation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs)**: The confirm_candidate() method validates a selected candidate by:\\n   - Unifying the candidate's trait ref with the obligation's trait ref\\n   - Collecting nested obligations from the impl\\n   - Returning nested PredicateObligations that must also be satisfied\\n   - Handling different candidate types (ImplCandidate, ParamCandidate, BuiltinCandidate, etc.)\\n\\n7. **Error Reporting (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs)**: When obligations cannot be fulfilled, the report_fulfillment_errors() method generates user-facing diagnostics. It:\\n   - Aggregates errors from failed obligations\\n   - Suggests potential fixes (add trait bounds, use type parameters, etc.)\\n   - Provides context about which impls were considered but rejected\\n   - Reports impl mismatch errors with detailed suggestions\\n\\nThe complete obligation chain works as follows:\\nFulfillmentContext::register_obligation() \u2192 FulfillmentContext::select() \u2192 ObligationForest::process_obligations() \u2192 FulfillProcessor::process_obligation() \u2192 SelectionContext::select() \u2192 assemble_candidates() \u2192 candidate filtering \u2192 confirm_candidate() \u2192 nested obligations \u2192 Error or Success \u2192 report_fulfillment_errors()\\n\\nWhen an obligation fails at any point (no matching impls, nested obligations fail, or type mismatch), the error flows back through the obligation tree, ultimately being reported via the error reporting system which provides helpful diagnostics to the user.\"\n}\n",
